## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (Duffing-type), damping (van der Pol-type), or through parametric/external forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (Duffing + nonlinear damping coupling)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic restoring force, asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x (broad nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²·v indicate amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of van der Pol or self-excited oscillators
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies; explicit t-dependence signals external driving or parametric excitation
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient of v) combined with positive cubic velocity damping (negative coefficient of v³) indicates limit cycle behavior
- Trigonometric functions of time (sin/cos of c·t) indicate periodic external forcing or parametric modulation rather than intrinsic dynamics
- A restoring force of form sin(x) or sinh(x) rather than polynomial suggests pendulum-like or relativistic oscillator geometry
- Products of velocity and even powers of position (v·x², v·x⁴) are signatures of energy-dependent dissipation mechanisms
- If the system is conservative (no v or t dependence), dv_dt should be expressible as the negative gradient of a potential: dv_dt = -dU/dx
